# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Consumer Heartbeat Session Timeout

## Your Task

Users report Kafka consumer groups drop membership with 'Heartbeat session timed out'. Find the Java source files in apache/kafka that (1) define the heartbeat session timeout threshold and (2) raise or log this timeout during the consumer polling loop.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

```json
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I've completed the analysis and created the answer file. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Findings

I've identified the Java source files in Apache Kafka that handle the heartbeat session timeout mechanism:

### Files Found:

1. **Heartbeat.java** - Defines the `sessionTimeoutExpired()` method that checks if the session timer has expired
2. **GroupRebalanceConfig.java** - Holds the `sessionTimeoutMs` configuration parameter
3. **CommonClientConfigs.java** - Defines the `SESSION_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG` configuration constant
4. **AbstractCoordinator.java** - Implements the heartbeat timeout detection during consumer polling in the `HeartbeatThread.run()` method
5. **GroupMetadataManager.java** - Implements server-side handling with `expireClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat()` to remove members when timeout occurs

### How It Works:

**Client-Side Detection:**
- The heartbeat timeout threshold is configured via `session.timeout.ms` (default 10 seconds)
- During consumer polling, the `Heartbeat.sessionTimeoutExpired()` method checks if no heartbeat response was received within the timeout period
- When timeout is detected, `AbstractCoordinator.HeartbeatThread.run()` (line 1513-1517) marks the coordinator as unknown, causing the consumer to drop group membership

**Server-Side Handling:**
- `GroupMetadataManager.expireClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat()` removes the member from the group when the broker's heartbeat timeout timer expires
- Logs message: "Member {memberId} in group {groupId} has failed, removing it from the group"

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with all relevant files, symbols, the call chain, and a detailed narrative explanation.

and removes members when they stop sending heartbeats.\\n\\n## Configuration Definition\\nThe heartbeat session timeout threshold is defined through the configuration parameter `SESSION_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG` in `CommonClientConfigs.java`. This configuration is extracted into `GroupRebalanceConfig.java` (line 41) which stores the `sessionTimeoutMs` value (line 52).\\n\\n## Client-Side Timeout Detection\\nOn the consumer client side, the `Heartbeat.java` class manages heartbeat timing. The `sessionTimeoutExpired()` method (lines 119-122) checks whether the session timer has expired by calling `sessionTimer.isExpired()`. This method is invoked during the consumer polling loop in the heartbeat thread.\\n\\nThe heartbeat timeout check occurs in `AbstractCoordinator.java` within the `HeartbeatThread.run()` method (lines 1513-1517). When `heartbeat.sessionTimeoutExpired(now)` returns true, the client marks the coordinator as unknown with the message \\\"session timed out without receiving a heartbeat response\\\". This causes the consumer group membership to drop as the client can no longer communicate with the group coordinator.\\n\\n## Server-Side Timeout Handling\\nOn the broker/group coordinator side, `GroupMetadataManager.java` implements `expireClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat()` (lines 6664-6702) which is invoked when a member's heartbeat session timeout expires. This method removes the member from the group and logs: \\\"Member {memberId} in group {groupId} has failed, removing it from the group\\\" (lines 6691-6692) or \\\"Pending member {memberId} in group {groupId} has been removed after session timeout expiration\\\" (lines 6682-6683).\\n\\n## Call Chain\\nThe complete flow is:\\n1. `Heartbeat.sessionTimeoutExpired()` detects the timeout on the client side\\n2. `AbstractCoordinator.HeartbeatThread.run()` detects this and calls `markCoordinatorUnknown()`\\n3. The consumer drops group membership\\n4. Server-side: `GroupMetadataManager.expireClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat()` removes the member and triggers rebalancing\\n\\nThe timeout value is controlled by the `session.timeout.ms` configuration (default 10 seconds), which must be set according to broker constraints defined by `group.min.session.timeout.ms` and `group.max.session.timeout.ms`.\"\n}\n",

This configuration is extracted into `GroupRebalanceConfig.java` (line 41) which stores the `sessionTimeoutMs` value (line 52).\\n\\n## Client-Side Timeout Detection\\nOn the consumer client side, the `Heartbeat.java` class manages heartbeat timing. The `sessionTimeoutExpired()` method (lines 119-122) checks whether the session timer has expired by calling `sessionTimer.isExpired()`. This method is invoked during the consumer polling loop in the heartbeat thread.\\n\\nThe heartbeat timeout check occurs in `AbstractCoordinator.java` within the `HeartbeatThread.run()` method (lines 1513-1517). When `heartbeat.sessionTimeoutExpired(now)` returns true, the client marks the coordinator as unknown with the message \\\"session timed out without receiving a heartbeat response\\\". This causes the consumer group membership to drop as the client can no longer communicate with the group coordinator.\\n\\n## Server-Side Timeout Handling\\nOn the broker/group coordinator side, `GroupMetadataManager.java` implements `expireClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat()` (lines 6664-6702) which is invoked when a member's heartbeat session timeout expires. This method removes the member from the group and logs: \\\"Member {memberId} in group {groupId} has failed, removing it from the group\\\" (lines 6691-6692) or \\\"Pending member {memberId} in group {groupId} has been removed after session timeout expiration\\\" (lines 6682-6683).\\n\\n## Call Chain\\nThe complete flow is:\\n1. `Heartbeat.sessionTimeoutExpired()` detects the timeout on the client side\\n2. `AbstractCoordinator.HeartbeatThread.run()` detects this and calls `markCoordinatorUnknown()`\\n3. The consumer drops group membership\\n4. Server-side: `GroupMetadataManager.expireClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat()` removes the member and triggers rebalancing\\n\\nThe timeout value is controlled by the `session.timeout.ms` configuration (default 10 seconds), which must be set according to broker constraints defined by `group.min.session.timeout.ms` and `group.max.session.timeout.ms`.\"\n}\n",
